  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f9f0346e-73c6-40cf-b970-d75e7b3a4716'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer15116376215951561346"><b>
  <u>EXPERIMENTAL READ OF THE MONTH: MAY 2016</u>
</b><br/><i>Every month my friends and I go out of our comfort zones and embrace the world outside historical and contemporary romance. Thanks for accompanying me on this wild ride, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/6378079-sraxe' rel='nofollow noopener'>sraxe</a>!</i><br/><br/><b>DNF@24%.</b><br/><br/>Let's play a guessing game. Why do you think sraxe and I both DNF-ed this book?<br/><b>A.</b> Because it's predictable as hell, and we found out who the killer was early on in the book<br/><b>B.</b> Because the main character, Katie, was an invertebrate with a non-existent personality<br/><b>C.</b> Because </span>
  <span id="freeText15116376215951561346" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>EXPERIMENTAL READ OF THE MONTH: MAY 2016</u>
</b><br /><i>Every month my friends and I go out of our comfort zones and embrace the world outside historical and contemporary romance. Thanks for accompanying me on this wild ride, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/6378079-sraxe" rel="nofollow noopener">sraxe</a>!</i><br /><br /><b>DNF@24%.</b><br /><br />Let's play a guessing game. Why do you think sraxe and I both DNF-ed this book?<br /><b>A.</b> Because it's predictable as hell, and we found out who the killer was early on in the book<br /><b>B.</b> Because the main character, Katie, was an invertebrate with a non-existent personality<br /><b>C.</b> Because the love interest, Richard, was a douchebag who kissed another woman later on in the book (granted, Richard and Katie weren't <i>officially</i> together, but hell, man, you were already putting the moves on her, you mofo)<br /><b>D.</b> Because the side characters were frustrating as fuck<br /><b>E.</b> Because the subject of cheating wasn't handled properly (the cheater even got a HEA with his mistress)<br /><b>F.</b> All of the above<br /><br />Oh, you answered F?<br /><br />Ding. Ding. Ding. We have a winner, folks!<br /><br />Your prize is that you get to avoid wasting your 6.99 USD on this crappy story. Congratulations!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460857015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7901100183205000004">Oh my God! These are the best words to describe this book. The story, the characters, the twists and turns that these book presents are amazing. It was incredibly difficult to put it down once I started reading it. The most impressive thing about this book is the fact that it starts right away with action, and it got me thinking "how in the world is this author gonna 'extend' the story for another 300 pages?" But she did it. I totally recommend it to anyone who likes crime books. And I most cert</span>
  <span id="freeText7901100183205000004" style="display:none">Oh my God! These are the best words to describe this book. The story, the characters, the twists and turns that these book presents are amazing. It was incredibly difficult to put it down once I started reading it. The most impressive thing about this book is the fact that it starts right away with action, and it got me thinking "how in the world is this author gonna 'extend' the story for another 300 pages?" But she did it. I totally recommend it to anyone who likes crime books. And I most certainly will read more books from this author.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1619554169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2675141852598420701">Well, that was quite a disappointment after the enjoyment of the last book. I even ended up DNFing this a quarter of the way in.<br/><br/>Although the last book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41487.No_Place_Like_Home' title='No Place Like Home by Mary Higgins Clark' rel='nofollow noopener'>No Place Like Home</a>, took some time to pick up, at least it kept my interest because of the likeable characters. I found myself rooting for certain individuals and suspecting who could be up to what. This book? I didn't like any of the key players and the whodunit wasn't a whodunit at all.<br/><br/>First off, Katie was a very, very weak character. She didn'</span>
  <span id="freeText2675141852598420701" style="display:none">Well, that was quite a disappointment after the enjoyment of the last book. I even ended up DNFing this a quarter of the way in.<br /><br />Although the last book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41487.No_Place_Like_Home" title="No Place Like Home by Mary Higgins Clark" rel="nofollow noopener">No Place Like Home</a>, took some time to pick up, at least it kept my interest because of the likeable characters. I found myself rooting for certain individuals and suspecting who could be up to what. This book? I didn't like any of the key players and the whodunit wasn't a whodunit at all.<br /><br />First off, Katie was a very, very weak character. She didn't even have any real personality in the quarter of the book I read. She kind of just meandered through the story. Literally every other character had more of an appeal and pull than she did. And isn't that saying something considering she's the main character, right?<br /><br />Another irritating part about her was her obsession with wanting to have children. She acted like it was the end of the fucking world if she couldn't have children. I know some women badly want bio kids, but it just really frustrates me having to actually read about it. There was millions of children out there who are in need of homes, and Katie here is sitting around being all <i>woe is me! I'll never be a mother!</i> It's not the end of the fucking world! Fucking adopt.<br /><br />And then, unlike the last book, I didn't even have any couple to cheer for in the end. Yeah, yeah, I know this isn't a romance book, but it's pretty obvious that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Richard and Katie are going to end up together (which I know for a fact because I skimmed to the end). But how could I even root for them when everything he did was so fucking unlikeable? And hearing about how he went off and was happy to entertain the many other "mighty attractive ladies who enjoyed his company well enough." No fucking thanks. What's there to cheer for when the guy hangs up without listening to her response, invites himself into her home, makes insensitive as fuck comments about Katie's late husband, etc etc etc. And he even ends up going on a date with some other woman in Chapter 24. No thanks. He was just completely unlikeable and there was nothing to cheer for there. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The mystery seemed like it was going to be a whodunit mystery, but it wasn't. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I thought, like the last book, we'd have to figure out who was the culprit. I even discarded some early suspicions because they felt like red herrings, but then the author was pretty much telling us who did it, so it just became boring. And it actually DID seem like it was going to be a murder mystery because the author made a point of having all of Highley's murdering POVs be just in male pronouns without his name being used. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And Chris <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and Joan end up together in the end? No fucking thanks to those cheating fuckers getting their HEA, especially after Chris kept quiet for a while about his suspicions on Vangie's "suicide" possibly being a murder. Like, this fucker ain't shit. She might have been insufferable, but he was cheating on her AND he resented the fact that she even got pregnant! The least he could fucking do is fess up immediately about what he thinks ACTUALLY happened to her. But noooooooooo. Asshole. DIAF! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There was nothing and no one to cheer for here.<br /><br />This was May's "Experimental Read of the Month" with my fellow Detective Amazing Hair, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/43278962-daniella" rel="nofollow noopener">Daniella</a>! At least we <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/95600239" rel="nofollow noopener">grumbled and moaned and cussed</a> about this book together, Dani.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2675141852598420701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1264684051" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1264684051" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2141067-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1282757192p2/2141067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1264684051?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/2141067-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780743206136" href="/book/show/7492165-the-cradle-will-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2141067-emma?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1264684051" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9114304418261830405">As I was reading this, my first MHC novel, I was thinking to myself, "this sounds like a Lifetime movie." Imagine my chagrin when I found out it WAS made into a Lifetime movie.<br/><br/>We get to see the story from many points of view, including the killer's, so there is never any mystery as to whodunit. Instead we spend the novel trying to figure out why. That was an interesting angle to come at it and I was pulled in by this novel. I hardly put it down all day and read it in just a couple sittings.<br/><br/>Overa</span>
  <span id="freeText9114304418261830405" style="display:none">As I was reading this, my first MHC novel, I was thinking to myself, "this sounds like a Lifetime movie." Imagine my chagrin when I found out it WAS made into a Lifetime movie.<br /><br />We get to see the story from many points of view, including the killer's, so there is never any mystery as to whodunit. Instead we spend the novel trying to figure out why. That was an interesting angle to come at it and I was pulled in by this novel. I hardly put it down all day and read it in just a couple sittings.<br /><br />Overall the quality wasn't very good, though. Why does MHC describe her characters by stating what famous actor or actress they look like? Not only does that seem monumentally lazy, it also dates the story.<br /><br /> There was quite a bit of cheesy dialogue. And misunderstood dialogue? Richard seemed like a total tool to me. What about that scene where he takes Kate to dinner and talks about himself the whole time? I was all, "wow. what a dirtbag." Then Katie is all, "this really made me think about my life and see Richard in a new light so now I think I love him." DO WHAT NOW? Plus, instalove. So, yeah.<br /><br />Previous reviewers mentioned crazy twists and turns but I didn't see them. They weren't very crazy or very twisty because the foreshadowing was too heavy handed, I saw it all coming and seriously, I am NOT one of those people that guesses a book's ending by page twelve. Generally I'm the most gullible, oblivious reader I've ever met. You can hit me with a two by four of foreshadowing and at the end I'll still be like, "OMG SNAPE KILLED DUMBLEDORE?!"<br /><br />Finally, it felt like the only plot device in this entire book was missed phone calls. Seriously missed phone calls were absolutely the cause of 100% of the mystery in The Cradle Will Fall. I guess that's the magic of the time before cell phones.<br /><br />This won't stop me from attempting a more recent MHC novel but I won't go into it with very high hopes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9114304418261830405" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2226556587" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2226556587" />
    <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas"><img alt="Benjamin Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451660582p2/4209082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2226556587?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Thomas" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780671741198" href="/book/show/740347.The_Cradle_Will_Fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=thriller-medical">thriller-medical</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2226556587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10543641986707891062">Continuing my December custom of cleaning off my shelves of those books that have been languishing for years, I turned to a random Mary Higgins Clark novel that I inherited from my mother who, judging from the sheer volume of them, must have loved. I remember reading a couple many years ago and considered them OK but nothing to write home about.<br/><br/>This one was only the third suspense novel published by the prolific Ms. Clark, first published in 1980. The plot was pretty straight-forward and concern</span>
  <span id="freeText10543641986707891062" style="display:none">Continuing my December custom of cleaning off my shelves of those books that have been languishing for years, I turned to a random Mary Higgins Clark novel that I inherited from my mother who, judging from the sheer volume of them, must have loved. I remember reading a couple many years ago and considered them OK but nothing to write home about.<br /><br />This one was only the third suspense novel published by the prolific Ms. Clark, first published in 1980. The plot was pretty straight-forward and concerns a rather diabolical OBGYN doctor who liked to experiment with fetuses. The news of the first in vitro fertilization (test-tube baby) in 1978 was still fresh in reader’s minds so I suppose the plot was timely. I actually enjoyed this one more than I expected, even though there were a lot of extraneous scenes with characters that didn’t seem to directly relate to the plot. The antagonist is known to the reader almost immediately but nevertheless, the story remained interesting and moved along at a fairly quick page-turning pace. The end was somewhat predictable but still satisfying.<br /><br />3.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="10543641986707891062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1927849908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1927849908" />
    <a title="Eli Easton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14978908-eli-easton"><img alt="Eli Easton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425767743p2/14978908.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1927849908?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eli Easton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eli Easton" href="/user/show/14978908-eli-easton">Eli Easton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1927849908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16863186122273094145">Read for my lifetime challenge (1980). This book was a bestseller in 1980 but I've never read it. I like medical thrillers, and thought the blurb sounded interesting.<br/><br/>This is quite a page-turner and a fun medical thriller. The medical component of the story revolves around a fertility doctor who is doing some unethical, and secret, procedures on his patients. I'm not going to get into the details of his procedures, since that's part of the mystery, but I'm not sure the science portion of the stor</span>
  <span id="freeText16863186122273094145" style="display:none">Read for my lifetime challenge (1980). This book was a bestseller in 1980 but I've never read it. I like medical thrillers, and thought the blurb sounded interesting.<br /><br />This is quite a page-turner and a fun medical thriller. The medical component of the story revolves around a fertility doctor who is doing some unethical, and secret, procedures on his patients. I'm not going to get into the details of his procedures, since that's part of the mystery, but I'm not sure the science portion of the story would hold up today. Still, if you are willing to accept that part of it, the story is a lot of fun.<br /><br />The plot is a long cat-and-mouse chase. The reader is informed right up front that the doctor is a murderer, willing to kill to protect his reputation and practice. But the police in the story have no idea, including the main character, Katie, who works for the prosecutor's office. She also happens to be a patient of the main nefarious doctor and is in direct danger from him throughout the book. But everyone thinks this doctor is just wonderful. There are a handful of murders in the book, starting with the kick-off scene and continuing through the plot as the doctor is forced to go further to guard his secrets. <br /><br />There are a number of convenient coincidences in the plot, such as Katie, one of the investigators, being the doctor's patient, and also a number of moments that go something like this: one character is about to tell another character a critical piece of info that will unravel the case and/or save Katie, but at the last second there's an interruption like someone walks in or there's a phone call, and that important info is never given. It happens so often it begins to strain credulity like hot taffy.<br /><br />Despite the eye-rolling this induces, it certainly effective at keeping the tension high and the pages turning. I was anxious for the bad guy to get caught and the heroine to be saved. Played like a fiddle: me. Twenty-seven years after this was a bestseller, it's still a super fun read. <br /><br />Recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16863186122273094145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2156424196" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2156424196" />
    <a title="Chris Norbury" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8144544-chris-norbury"><img alt="Chris Norbury" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539371331p2/8144544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2156424196?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Norbury" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Norbury" href="/user/show/8144544-chris-norbury">Chris Norbury</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7889616-the-cradle-will-fall">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2156424196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3351575734230215837">I think this was my first MHC read (may have read one or two decades ago), and I was quite disappointed. Considering it was only her fourth novel, I expected a much higher quality of prose than I received. The dialogue was stiff and lame. Characters lacked any likeability. First names were overused in dialogue to the point of annoyance in places. Knowing early on who the bad guy was eliminated most of the tension and suspense. As others have said in their reviews, if only all the players had got</span>
  <span id="freeText3351575734230215837" style="display:none">I think this was my first MHC read (may have read one or two decades ago), and I was quite disappointed. Considering it was only her fourth novel, I expected a much higher quality of prose than I received. The dialogue was stiff and lame. Characters lacked any likeability. First names were overused in dialogue to the point of annoyance in places. Knowing early on who the bad guy was eliminated most of the tension and suspense. As others have said in their reviews, if only all the players had gotten together and shared what they knew with each other, the case would have been solved in five minutes.<br /><br />More importantly, I couldn't tell who the protagonist was. It should have been Katie DeMaio, but she played this limp, helpless character whose primary concern was getting her D and C done so she could get on with her life. Richard Carroll was by default the protagonist because he at least tried to solve the question of who killed Vangie Lewis, but he was only the medical examiner. The police characters were mere shells of characters and didn't seem to have much of a plan or care much whether or not they solved the murder. And Dr. Highley, the antagonist, was merely psychotically annoying, although he at least had a strong motivation for his actions.<br /><br />My overall assessment of this book is that MHC broke through with her first bestseller, signed a contract for two or three more books (of which this was #2) and cranked it out under considerable pressure to meet a publishing deadline. Very disappointing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3351575734230215837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2156424196">
  <td colspan="2">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3425240055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4231912544557152065">I needed a book to read while visiting my parents. My mom had this book lying around so I took the bait. Mary Higgins Clark has been dubbed the queen of suspense, she is a pioneer in her field, and I actually really enjoyed her biography, but after you have read a few of her books, they all seem so tiringly similar: a single, white, successful, sophisticated NY women becomes entangled with a psychotic man. There will always be a blundering single, overweight, middle aged woman, who comes from a </span>
  <span id="freeText4231912544557152065" style="display:none">I needed a book to read while visiting my parents. My mom had this book lying around so I took the bait. Mary Higgins Clark has been dubbed the queen of suspense, she is a pioneer in her field, and I actually really enjoyed her biography, but after you have read a few of her books, they all seem so tiringly similar: a single, white, successful, sophisticated NY women becomes entangled with a psychotic man. There will always be a blundering single, overweight, middle aged woman, who comes from a lower income setting, who will unintentionally blotch the case by her reckless desire to have something exciting happen in her mundane life. The last predictable character will generally be an attractive single, white man somehow professionally involved in solving the case. You know right where this is going, everyone knows where a Mary Higgins Clark book is going. I believe her reign as Queen of suspense was over decades ago. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4231912544557152065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13831393002343590148">The cover of this book says "The Terrifying National Bestseller.." Don' believe every thing you read. This was the first Mary Higgins Clark novel I have read and frankly it most likely will be my last. The reason being, I absolutely hate it when authors are repetitive and she repeats thoughts, fears, ect. repeatedly. The book could have been much shorter, much cleaner had she not written repeatedly of Katie Deaio's fear of hospitals or Dr. Highly's plan to kill her in a hospital. Clark's portray</span>
  <span id="freeText13831393002343590148" style="display:none">The cover of this book says "The Terrifying National Bestseller.." Don' believe every thing you read. This was the first Mary Higgins Clark novel I have read and frankly it most likely will be my last. The reason being, I absolutely hate it when authors are repetitive and she repeats thoughts, fears, ect. repeatedly. The book could have been much shorter, much cleaner had she not written repeatedly of Katie Deaio's fear of hospitals or Dr. Highly's plan to kill her in a hospital. Clark's portrayal of blooming love between Katie and Richard Carroll was rather sophmoric and absolutely not needed for the story. The main plot of the story was interesting and the story could have been woven to be much more suspenseful but as it was after awhile I just wanted the book to be over.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3180990411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10711029212687082554">Mary Higgins Clark third book wasn't as great as the first two. Still good but I know why I don't really remember much about it. It begins with prosecutor Katie DeMaio getting into a car accident. While recovering in hospital she spies someone dumping something into the trunk of a car. At first it looks like a bundle but then the blanket opens revealing the face of a dead woman. This sighting will seal Katie's fate. Dr. Edgar Highley a medical genius has much to hide. Including dark experiments </span>
  <span id="freeText10711029212687082554" style="display:none">Mary Higgins Clark third book wasn't as great as the first two. Still good but I know why I don't really remember much about it. It begins with prosecutor Katie DeMaio getting into a car accident. While recovering in hospital she spies someone dumping something into the trunk of a car. At first it looks like a bundle but then the blanket opens revealing the face of a dead woman. This sighting will seal Katie's fate. Dr. Edgar Highley a medical genius has much to hide. Including dark experiments on his patients. Women who thought they would never ha e babies find themselves pregnant while under the care of Dr. Highley. Vangie Lewis was one, but she is found dead of an apparent suicide. But something doesn't add up for investigators and an autopsy threatens to unravel Dr. Highley and his thriving practice. Soon Katie begins to think it was Vangie she saw in the trunk of the car, but not knowing the culprit or if it was real or a bad dream, she agrees to let Dr. Highley operate on her for a D&amp;C. As I mentioned not my favourite it probably wasn't back when I first read it either. Richard was the worst for a love interest and the relationship felt forced, Katie was okay, Edna was an idiot, like all those idiots in horror movies who end up dying because of their own stupidity, not really a mystery because we know damn well who the killer was from page one and it was more about figuring out what was going on in the medical practice. It's not a bad book, but it was one that didn't grab me like the first two I read did. So now I've finished volume one of my Mary Higgins Clark collection time for a bit of a break before I start another round of my trip down memory lane Mary Higgins Clark edition.</span>

<div id="review_2761787307" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2761787307" />
    <a title="Chris Demer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5619631-chris-demer"><img alt="Chris Demer" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2761787307?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Demer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Demer" href="/user/show/5619631-chris-demer">Chris Demer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5619631-chris-demer?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5619631-chris-demer?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2761787307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17639346232003235282">A dated (1980)Murder mystery which, despite some issues, manages to hold the reader's interest.<br/><br/>A famous and highly regarded obstetrician/gynecologist with past, is helping desperate women to become mothers.But Katie De Maio, a local prosecutor involved in a minor traffic accident, is in the hospital and unable to sleep. In looking out the window to the parking lot below, believes she sees a man carrying the body of a woman to the trunk of his car and drive away in the middle of the night. <br/>The ne</span>
  <span id="freeText17639346232003235282" style="display:none">A dated (1980)Murder mystery which, despite some issues, manages to hold the reader's interest.<br /><br />A famous and highly regarded obstetrician/gynecologist with past, is helping desperate women to become mothers.But Katie De Maio, a local prosecutor involved in a minor traffic accident, is in the hospital and unable to sleep. In looking out the window to the parking lot below, believes she sees a man carrying the body of a woman to the trunk of his car and drive away in the middle of the night. <br />The next day, one of Dr. Highley's patients is found dead at her home -of cyanide poisoning.<br />At first, assumed to be a suicide, multiple factors start to point to the possibility of murder.As the plot unfolds, the dead woman's husband is considered as the likely murderer, but through a tangle of events and players, the focus of the investigation changes. <br /><br />The plot is fairly trite and the author imposes her views (not that subtly) onto the plot which is irritating. (specifically, her take on abortion, "socialized" medicine, and petty criminals).<br /><br />She also starts chapters using pronouns such as he, she... and it is not clear who she is referring to until the second or third paragraph.<br /><br />In addition, even taking into consideration the date of the book, the author's knowledge of certain aspects of medicine seem sketchy. More research might have been helpful.<br /><br />Well I bought the paperback from my local library for $0.25, and read it on a vacation. So it served its purpose.<br />Good for beach reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17639346232003235282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3581908197?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelley" href="/user/show/1100764-shelley">Shelley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3581908197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer740927001032350161">My cover of The Cradle Will Fall is scary and freaky: it’s a bunch of naked dolls in the shadows. It's great!<br/><br/>Mary Higgins Clark is the Queen of Suspense. She didn’t fail me in this novel. It grabbed my attention right away, and never let up. It was fast paced and a great read. <br/><br/>The Cradle Will Fall is Mary Higgins Clark's third book she wrote 40 years ago in 1980 in the very early days of vitro fertilization. The 1st one took place in 1978, so it would had been a hot topic to write about back the</span>
  <span id="freeText740927001032350161" style="display:none">My cover of The Cradle Will Fall is scary and freaky: it’s a bunch of naked dolls in the shadows. It's great!<br /><br />Mary Higgins Clark is the Queen of Suspense. She didn’t fail me in this novel. It grabbed my attention right away, and never let up. It was fast paced and a great read. <br /><br />The Cradle Will Fall is Mary Higgins Clark's third book she wrote 40 years ago in 1980 in the very early days of vitro fertilization. The 1st one took place in 1978, so it would had been a hot topic to write about back then. <br /><br />Katie DeMalo is a county prosecutor. She’s also the main character. She ends up in hospital overnight as a result of a minor road accident. Looking out the window of her room, she isn’t sure she is seeing if what she is seeing is for real, or it’s a result of her half-conscious state. What she thinks she sees is a man loading a woman’s body into the truck of a car. The next day she begins investigating a suicide that looks more like it was murder. <br /><br />There is no mystery for the reader to solve. The killer is told to us at the very beginning, though we are not told why he is killing women. We slowly find that out as the story progresses. He is fertility doctor, Dr. Highley, and he is doing some unethical and secret procedures on his patients without their knowledge<br /><br />Katie ends up being a patient of Dr. Highley, not realizing she is in danger. And that’s where I end. I’m not saying anymore. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="740927001032350161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2087298992" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2087298992" />
    <a title="Jim C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c"><img alt="Jim C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340034171p2/10296231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2087298992?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim C" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c">Jim C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2087298992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11441779823700190101"><b>Actual rating is 3.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>This is your basic medical suspense thriller novel. In this one, Katie and her office is investigating the apparent suicide of a pregnant woman. Katie was in the hospital when she saw this dead woman being loaded into a trunk of a car. There is something fishy going on at the hospital.<br/><br/>I am sucker for a medical thriller and this one did not disappoint. This was pretty much straight forward as we knew the identity of the killer from the start. We did not know why he was </span>
  <span id="freeText11441779823700190101" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating is 3.5 stars.</b><br /><br />This is your basic medical suspense thriller novel. In this one, Katie and her office is investigating the apparent suicide of a pregnant woman. Katie was in the hospital when she saw this dead woman being loaded into a trunk of a car. There is something fishy going on at the hospital.<br /><br />I am sucker for a medical thriller and this one did not disappoint. This was pretty much straight forward as we knew the identity of the killer from the start. We did not know why he was doing it. The thing with a medical thriller is the belief of the pseudo science and I bought into it here. I liked the characters and I especially liked their interactions with each other. I did have one little problem with this book. It seemed like every character in the book had a connection with every character or the happenings of the book. It did extend the laws of plausibility. Or it really is a small world a everyone is connected to everyone. It didn't take away my enjoyment but I did question it.<br /><br />This is a simple medical thriller book that is a prime example of a beach read. I held my interest throughout and there were a couple of twists that did catch me by surprise.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11441779823700190101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny Kay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny Kay" href="/user/show/52103443-jenny-kay">Jenny Kay</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2654803563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5203838360315039783">This was my first Mary Higgins Clark. She is known as the "Queen of Suspense", but I think a more fitting title would be "Godmother of Chick-Lit". If I had read this book before all of last year's selections of suspense novels featuring women in peril, I likely would have rated it higher. As it is, because she has inspired so many insipid, formulaic copycats I had the displeasure of reading, the usual, predictable and boring stakes of babies and marriages is not so gripping.<br/><br/>A criticism I've seen</span>
  <span id="freeText5203838360315039783" style="display:none">This was my first Mary Higgins Clark. She is known as the "Queen of Suspense", but I think a more fitting title would be "Godmother of Chick-Lit". If I had read this book before all of last year's selections of suspense novels featuring women in peril, I likely would have rated it higher. As it is, because she has inspired so many insipid, formulaic copycats I had the displeasure of reading, the usual, predictable and boring stakes of babies and marriages is not so gripping.<br /><br />A criticism I've seen about this book is that we know who the murderer is right off the bat. I don't have a problem with this because whodunnit is not as intriguing as the "why?". For that reason alone, that the woman in peril is not imperiled by her significant other, I give it a middle of the road rating instead of 1 or 2 stars.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText510709396909358126" style="display:none">My FIRST Mary Higgins Clark. Say What!?! I know. Crazy. This is a super throwback to the year of...umm...my birth..ahem...yes, that.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YYKp5i6JAZ6EjVralnfbNaLrrCKikgY639HpdcXQyFvLi/jh5hHu5sanNwa2jlPLSvbkbB49rpyvJHijySovVg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6Xjc4hpqQw86vDq//de4d473VCT1bB2RjAmbz+sS/OhDcY3l0vKsd3iWV2PdLjCJZuocaknDtTf8/AoZ5+gb5Q==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12107425472645647104">The #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author Mary Higgins Clark has written thirty-eight suspense novels, four collections of short stories, a his­torical novel, a memoir, and two children’s books. With bestselling author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108774._Alafair_Burke' title=' Alafair Burke' rel='nofollow noopener'> Alafair Burke</a> she wrote the Under Suspicion series. With her daughter <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12454._Carol_Higgins_Clark' title=' Carol Higgins Clark' rel='nofollow noopener'> Carol Higgins Clark</a>, she has coauthored five more suspense novels. <br/><br/>Clark’s books have sold more than 100 milli</span>
  <span id="freeText12107425472645647104" style="display:none">The #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author Mary Higgins Clark has written thirty-eight suspense novels, four collections of short stories, a his­torical novel, a memoir, and two children’s books. With bestselling author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108774._Alafair_Burke" title=" Alafair Burke" rel="nofollow noopener"> Alafair Burke</a> she wrote the Under Suspicion series. With her daughter <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12454._Carol_Higgins_Clark" title=" Carol Higgins Clark" rel="nofollow noopener"> Carol Higgins Clark</a>, she has coauthored five more suspense novels. <br /><br />Clark’s books have sold more than 100 million copies in the United States alone. Her books are beloved around the world and made her an international bestseller many times over.</span>
